Jamison Brereton

127
Agni
Paruchepa Daivod─Бsi
11 verses: atyaс╣гс╣нi, except atidhr╠еti 6
Full of puns, phonological tricks, and syntactic give-and-take, this hymn celebrates Agni in both his ritual role (e.g., vss. 1тАУ2, 8, 10) and in his physical power (e.g., vss. 3тАУ4, 6). The pleasures of the hymn come more from the interplay of the verbal ele ments than from any sustained thematic development, and in that sense GeldnerтАЩs тАЬgedankenarmтАЭ (quoted above) may be accurate, but who needs thoughts when we have such words?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI venerate Agni, the invoker (of the gods), the munificent, the giver of dwellings, the son of strength; he who knows all that exists, like a sage who is endowed with knowledge; who, the divine regenerator of sacrifices, through his lofty and reverntial devotion, covets for the gods the blaze of the liquefied butter which is offered in oblation with his flames.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Atyaс╣гс╣нi is a stanza of four lines, and has 68 syllables. The metrical system of the Vedas, or Chandas has a graduated series of metres. Utkс╣Ыti has 104 syllables and descends by a diminution of four through eight classes to atyaс╣гс╣нi, the ninth, which gives it 68 syllables. In this s┼лkta, the hymns are arranged in three verses and the number fo syllables vary from 57 to 70, the average being 65 to 67

Jamison Brereton

Agni I consider as the Hotar, rich in gifts, the good one, son of strength, J─БtavedasтАФlike a poet, J─БtavedasтАФ
who is the god of good ceremony, with his body erect and pointed
toward the gods.
With his flame he yearns after the blazing forth of the gheeтАФof the melted butter being poured.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The patterned connections of the 8-syllable p─Бdas to their preceding p─Бdas are detailed in the published introduction. to this hymn group.

Griffith

AGNI I hold as herald, the munificent, the gracious, Son of Strength, who knoweth all that live, as holy Singer, knowing all,
Lord of fair rites, a God with form erected turning to the Gods,
He, when the flame hath sprung forth from the holy oil, the offered fatness, longeth for it with his glow.

Oldenberg

I deem Agni to be the munificent Hotri, the Vasu, the Son of strength 1, G├вtavedas, like a priest, G├вtavedas 2: the best performer of the sacrifice, the god who with his upright body that is turned towards the gods, and with his flame longs for the shine of the (boiling) ghee 3, of the butter that is offered in (the fire).

Geldner

Den Agni erachte ich als den Hotri, den freigebigen Gott, den Sohn der Kraft, den Jatavedas, den Gott, der mit seiner aufrechten, gottw├дrts gerichteten Gestalt den Gottesdienst gut versieht. Mit seiner Glut verlangt er nach dem Aufflammen des Schmalzes, der geopferten Schmelzbutter.

Grassmann

Den Agni ehr’ als gabenreichen Priester ich, den Wesenkenner als den guten Sohn der Kraft, als S├дnger den, der Wesen kennt; Sch├╢n opfernd steht mit seinem Leib zu G├╢ttern strebend hoch der Gott; Dem Gl├╝hn der Butter eilt mit seiner Glut er nach, des ausgegossnen fetten Tranks.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe, the instrumental tutors of the ceremony, invoke you, Agni, who are most deserving of worship, and are the eldest of the Aс╣Еgirasas, with (acceptable) prayers; and with prayers (recited) by the priests, (we adore) you, who, like the traverser of the sky, (the sun), are the invoker (of the gods on behalf) of men, and whom, the bright-haired showeree (of blessings), many people approaching propitiate for the attainment of felicity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We sacrificers would invoke you as best sacrificer, the oldest of the Aс╣Еgirases, o poet, with our thoughtsтАФ(invoke you) through our poets, o glowing one, with our thoughtsтАФ
(you) like earth-encircling heaven, the Hotar of the settled domains, the flame-haired bull whom these clans (help)тАФlet the clans help (him) to speed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although тАЬearth-encircling heavenтАЭ fits easily into our modern cosmology, I donтАЩt know what is meant by this in a Vedic cosmological context. This problem clearly troubles both Geldner and Renou, who both supply the sun to do the circling, with heaven as the object (Renou: тАЬLui qui circule autour (de lтАЩaire) comme (le soleil autour du) cielтАЭ). Although I understand the impetus, these interpr. introduce too much extra machinery into a simple two-word simile.

Agni was compared to a v├нpra- in 1c and then addressed as one in 2b. In 2c we invoke Agni with our own v├нpra-s, with v├нprebhiс╕е occuping the same position as v├нpram in 1c. This type of implicit identification between Agni and his mortal worshipers is also found in 2a, where we sacrificers (y├бjam─Бn─Бс╕е) invoke him as best sacrificer (y├бjiс╣гс╣нham).

2f is a relative clause that lacks a verb; the verb ([pra-]├бvanti vel sim.) can be supplied from the verb in the 8-syllable tag (2g), which contains the impv. pr─Б╠Бvantu with the same subj. (v├н┼Ыaс╕е тАШclansтАЩ). The g-p─Бda also adds an infinitival dat. to this verbal complex, indicating what the clans help Indra to do. Constructing the verb in 2f from the one in 2g is not a matter of simple gapping, because imperatives cannot appear in relative clauses. Geldner supplies a different verb in f (huldigen) from that in g (ermutigen), but this ignores the patterned interplay characteristic of the 8-syllable p─Бdas with what precedes them.

Griffith

We, sacrificing, call on thee best worshipper, the eldest of Angirases, Singer, with hymns, thee, brilliant One! with singers’ hymns;
Thee, wandering round as ’t were the sky, who art the invoking Priest of men,
Whom, Bull with hair of flame the people must observe, the people that he speed them on.

Oldenberg

May we, the sacrificers, call thee hither, the best of sacrificers 1, the first of the Aс╣Еgiras, O priest, with our prayers, with priestly prayers, O bright one 2: thee who like the heaven encompassest the earth 3, the Hotri of human tribes, the manly flame-haired, whom these folksтАФwhom all folks should favour in order to speed him (to our sacrifice).

Geldner

Dich, den besten Opferer, wollen wir Opfernden rufen, den Obersten der Angiras, du Redekundiger, mit Gebeten, durch die Redekundigen mit Gebeten, du Heller. Den Hotri der V├╢lker, der die Opferst├дtte umkreist wie die Sonne den Himmel, den flammenhaarigen Bullen, dem diese St├дmme huldigen. Die St├дmme sollen ihn zur Eile ermutigen.

Grassmann

Die besten Opfrer rufen wir, die opfernden, mit Liedern, weiser, dich den besten Angiras, mit weisen Liedern, reiner, dich, Der du der Menschen Priester bist und ringsum gehst dem Himmel gleich, Den flammenhaar’gen Stier, den dieses Menschenvolk zur Eile treib’, das Menschenvolk.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬVerily, that Agni, far shining with brilliant vigour, is the destroyer of foes, like a hatchet that cuts down trees; whatever is most solid and stable dissolves like water at his contact; unsparing, he sports (amidst enemies), nor desists (from their destruction), like an archer who retreats not (frombattle).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Because he, shining upon the many with his radiant might, becomes the overcomer of deceitтАФthe overcomer of deceit, as an axe is an
excellent striker of woodтАФ
at whose attack even the staunch aborts and whatever is solid, like
the trees,
going forth to conquer, he will hold his place, he will not be movedтАФ with his conquering of the wastelands, he will not be moved.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse is richly studded with problems. One of the lesser ones is the referent and grammatical identity of pur┼л╠Бin the first p─Бda. Grassmann classifies it with singular (presumably NA neut.) forms; Geldner takes it as an adv. тАШgar sehrтАЩ; Witzel Got┼Н as instr.

sg. (?) with ├│jas─Б (тАЬmit ohnehin viel тАж K├╢rperkraftтАЭ). On the basis of the sequence (3d) v─лс╕╖├║ cid, (4a) dс╣Ыс╕╖h─Б╠Бcid, (4f) sthir─Б╠Бcid (also with ├│jas─Б), all containing neuters, most plural, I take pur┼л╠Бas the neut. pl. it appears to be (so also Renou: тАЬqui brille en maint endroitтАЭ). Each instance of cid тАШevenтАЩ in this sequence emphasizes the formidable targets Agni is exercising his will upon. Unfortunately this value of cid is not so much in evidence in our phrase pur┼л╠Бcid тАж d─л╠Бdy─Бnaс╕е because тАШshiningтАЩ (at least as expressed with the root тИЪd─л) is not ordinarily a forceful or hostile act. I have therefore (reluctantly) not rendered the cid here, though I feel I have missed something, since the phrasal parallelism is otherwise so clear. Perhaps d─л╠Бdy─Бnaс╕е has something of the sense of similar forms of тИЪ┼Ыuc тАШblaze (against)тАЩ: so тАЬshining (against) even the many with his radiant might.тАЭ P─Бda b and its tag-p─Бda c contains a ┼Ыleс╣гa, whose correct interpretation goes back at least to Benfey (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 3c). As indicated in the published introduction. to I.127-139, druhaс╣Гtar├бс╕е has two possible analyses: druhaс╣Г-tar├б- тАШovercoming deceitтАЩ or druhantara- тАШbetter at striking woodтАЩ. The first is appropriate to the first instance of the word, but in c the presence of para┼Ы├║с╕е тАШaxтАЩ forces the тАШwoodтАЩ interpr.

The verb of de, ┼Ыr├║vat, is the problem in that clause. Wh (Roots) takes it as a (zero-grade) 1st class pres. to тИЪsru тАШflowтАЩ, but тИЪsru has no such zero-gr. formations (and thereтАЩs the problem of the initial sibliant of course). Grassmann puts it with a root тИЪ┼Ыru тАШzerinnen, zergehenтАЩ (separate from тИЪ┼Ыru тАШhearтАЩ), but the formations he assigns to said тАЬrootтАЭ are a hodgepodge (and see Oldenberg on the likely nonexistence of the root). Renou (flg. Cardona, see RenouтАЩs n.) takes it to тИЪ┼Ыru тАШhearтАЩ, but this requires supplying the verb of destruction (by his interpr. тАШfallтАЩ) required by the context, with the perception verb that is actually found in the passage superfluous: тАЬon les entend (tomber) тАжтАЭ (The same root assignment seems to underlie the Witzel Got┼Н tr., though with a different overall interpr., which I confess I donтАЩt understand.) Even if the semantics worked better, there are no such stems to тИЪ┼Ыru тАШhearтАЩ. Geldner attributes it to тИЪ┼Ыс╣Э тАШcrushтАЩ, which is reasonable on both semantic and textual grounds; see esp. the parallel he cites X.89.6 ┼Ыс╣Ыс╣З─Б╠Бti v─лс╕╖├║ ruj├бti sthir─Б╠Бс╣Зi, with very similar phraseology. Unfortunately I can see no way to get a stem ┼Ыr├║va- from ┼Ыс╣Э. Oldenberg questioningly suggests a connection with тИЪru тАШbreakтАЩ, but needless to say the initial ┼Ы canтАЩt simply be omitted. I dare to suggest yet another root: тИЪsr─лv тАШabortтАЩ. Although some forms of this root (caus. srevayet [KS], RVic part. srev├бyant-; aor. asr─Бv─лt [JB]; pres. sr─лvyati [AB]) have an initial dental sibilant, others have the palatal: AV ┼Ыr─лvay─Бmi, MS ┼Ыr─лvayeyuс╕е, ┼Ыrevuka-. (On the forms, see Narten [Sig.Aor.] 282-83. Jamison [├бya-] 145.) Such phonetic fluctuation is not surprising in a root that presumably was at least partially tabooed. Although a stem ┼Ыr├║va- or sr├║va- is not otherwise found to this root, the spotty attestation to this root in general makes its isolation unsurprising. The stem would probably be a zerograde thematic injunctive (aor. or pres.?), though a root subjunctive canтАЩt be ruled out (though less likely in context). The loss of the i ╠п/ i would follow the same pattern as тИЪd─лv / d(y)┼л, тИЪs─лv / s(y)┼л, via *sRi ╠пuH ├а *sRuH. I do not understand the accent, however. As for тАШabortionтАЩ in this context of destruction, see, inter alia, the use of the caus. part. srev├бyant- in VII.18.8, the Battle of the Ten Kings; possibly also ├бva тИЪsru in nearby I.129.6.

The final two p─Бdas (fg) of this verse also present their share of difficulties.

We can begin with the final word of each p─Бda, n─Б╠Бyate in the Saс╣Гhit─Б text. The Pp.

(followed by Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition) analyses this as n├б ayate, but this produces a very bad cadence: we should expect a heavy syllable as the first syllable of the verb. This is easily remedied, without emending the Saс╣Гhit─Б text, by ─Б╠Бyate (i.e., prev. ─Б╠Б+ ayate). This analysis was also tentatively suggested by Got┼Н (1st cl., 92 n. 10).

Most tr. (and Oldenberg) take the point of yamate n─Б╠Бyate to be that though Agni is victorious, he doesnтАЩt go further: he stays in his hearth. See, e.g., Renou тАЬ’(Bien que) triomphant, il tient (les r├иnes), il ne va pas (plus loin).тАЭ But the preverb n├нс╕е тАШforthтАЩ (with тИЪsah only here and in the root noun niс╣гс╣г├бh-) seems to presuppose motion (hence my тАШgoing forth to conquerтАЩ), and certainly most treatments of Agni victorious depict him laying waste to his surroundings, as in the immediately preceding two p─Бdas and in the following verse (4). The notion that Agni is suddenly showing self-restraint here seems contrary to the message of the context. I therefore take yamate as meaning not тАШhold himself backтАЩ, but тАШhold/keep his placeтАЩ (against counterattack) and ─Б╠Бyate (/ayate) as a quasi-passive тАШbe movedтАЩ. Medial forms of тИЪi are rare enough that a consistent meaning to such a stem is hard to determine, and though some forms of ├бyate probably belong to a thematized stem (so Got┼Н, 92ff.), the parallelism with the root aor. subj. yamate here strongly suggests that our form is also a subjunctive (to the root pres. ├йti) and thus further separated from the thematic indicative forms. I therefore think that the somewhat idiosyncratic meaning I have attributed to the form is plausible, esp. as a negated semantic twin to yamate.

The final problem in the verse is the cmpd. instr. sg. dhanv─Бs├бh─Б. This is almost universally (Grassmann, Oldenberg, Geldner, Renou, Scarlatta 603) interpreted as тАШconquering with a bowтАЩ (dh├бnvan-), which interpr. generally requires an additional personage to be supplied, generally Rudra. Got┼Н (1st cl., 92, n. 10) seems to favor this interpr., but also suggests the possibility that the first member is dh├бnvan- тАШLandтАЩ: тАЬauf dem das Land ersiegenden [Weg],тАЭ with the whole p─Бda meaning that Agni will not go further and burn the land. Witzel Got┼Н have adopted this latter interpr. (though the тАШbowтАЩ interpr. is referred to in the n.): тАЬAuf dem trockenen Land ersiegenden (Weg) eilt er nicht hierher.тАЭ I am also convinced that dh├бnvan- тАШwastelandтАЩ is the correct interpr. of the 1st member. Given that the тАШtreeтАЩ theme is prominent in this verse and a тАШbowтАЩ theme lacking, a reference to another landscape feature fits the context better. There is the problem that cmpds with -s├бh- are ordinarily adjectives modifying animates (see the numerous exx. in Scarlatta.), and my tr. assumes an abstract sense or at the very least an instr. manner adverb (тАЬin/with his wasteland-conquering [manner]тАЭ). Despite this slight difficulty, this solution seems more economical than inserting Rudra into a context that has no other allusion to him.

I.127.3-4: In the published translation ├│jas─Б in 3a and 4f should have been tr. the same, rather than тАШmightтАЩ and тАШstrengthтАЩ respectively.

Griffith

He with his shining glory blazing far and wide, he verily it is who slayeth demon foes, slayeth the demons like an axe:
At whose close touch things solid shake, and what is stable yields like trees.
Subduing all, he keeps his ground and flinches not, from the skilled archer flinches not.

Oldenberg

He indeed, shining mightily with his shining strength 1, becomes the conqueror of deceitful foes 2тАФlike an axe, the conqueror of deceitful foes 2. He at whose onslaught 3 even what is strong melts away 4, steady things (waste away) like forests (which are burnt or bend down in the storm) 5. Conquering he holds himself back; he does not proceed 6. As with a conquering bow-man he proceeds 6.

Geldner

Denn er, der gar sehr mit strahlender Kraft leuchtet, ist der Unhold├╝berwinder, wie eine Axt der Unhold├╝berwinder und der Baumf├дller, bei dessen Anprall auch das Harte bricht, das Feste wie B├дume. Siegreich l├д├Яt er sich lenken, geht nicht durch; von dem Bogensieger gelenkt geht er nicht durch.

Grassmann

Denn er, der viel mit seiner flammenreichen Kraft bestrahlt, er ist es, welcher die D├дmonen tilgt, D├дmonen tilget wie ein Beil, Bei dessen Andrang auch das harte schnell zerfliesst, wie Wasserflut das feste auch; Den Sieg gewinnend h├дlt er Stand, nicht weicht er je, vor starkem Sch├╝tzen weicht er nicht.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThey have presented substantial donations to him, as (they give riches) to a sage, and by resplendent means he grants us (grace) for our preservation; (the worshipper) presents (gifts) to Agni for preservation; he who pervades the (many offerings made to him) consumes them (as rapidly) as (he consumes) forests; he matures the standing corn by his potency; he destroys whatever (things) are stationary by his potency.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He destroys whatever: sthir─Бс╣Зi ni riс╣З─Бtiajas─Б: sthir─Бс╣Зi = p─Бp─Бni, sins (amitr─Бс╣Зi, enemies)

Jamison Brereton

Even the firm things give way to him, as is known. (The pious one) does service with the piercingly hot kindling sticks, for helpтАФhe does
service to Agni for help.
He who plunges toward the many, he carves them with his flame
like trees.
Even solid foods he liquefies with his strengthтАФeven the solid with his strength.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I generate the subject тАЬ(the pious man),тАЭ i.e., d─Б┼Ыv─Б╠Бn, from its verb d─Бс╣гс╣нi.

Griffith

To him, as one who knows, even things solid yield: unrough fire-sticks heated hot he gives his gifts to aid. Men offer Agni gifts for aid.
He deeply piercing many a thing hews it like wood with fervent glow.
Even hard and solid food he crunches with his might, yea, hard and solid food with might.

Oldenberg

Even what is firm gives way before him: thus it is known. With hottest kindling-sticks 1 one worships him 2 for winning his favour, one worships Agni for winning his favour. He who dives into many forests as if carving the wood with his flame, destroys even firm food 3 with his strengthтАФhe destroys even what is firm with his strength.

Geldner

Selbst das Feste gibt ihm, wie man wei├Я, nach. Mit den am schnellsten feuerfangenden Reibh├╢lzern wartet er auf, um seine Gunst zu gewinnen, wartet er dem Agni auf, um seine Gunst zu gewinnen. Der in viele H├╢lzer eindringt, sie wie die B├дume mit seiner Flamme behauend; er zerrei├Яt selbst die festen Speisen mit Kraft, selbst das Feste mit Kraft.

Grassmann

Das feste selbst, es gibt ihm nach, so wie er ist; mit heissentflammten H├╢lzern dient man ihm um Gunst, dem Agni huldigt man um Gunst; In vieles dringt er und behaut die B├дume gleichsam mit der Glut. Die festen Speisen selbst zermalmet er mit Kraft, das feste selbst mit seiner Kraft.

Elizarenkova

рдлрд┐рд░ рдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдзреАрд╢реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХреИрд╕реЗ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ ред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe plural ce near the altar the (sacrificial) food of him who is more conspicuous by night than by day; (we offer it) to him who is scarcely alive by day; hence his (sacrificial) food finds prompt acceptance, like dwelling (given by a father) to a son; these undecaying fires, (although) discriminating between the devout and the undevout, grant (both) protection, and accepting (the offerings of the pious), they are exempt from decay.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Apr─Бyuс╣гe div─Бtar─Бt (Taittir─лya ─Аraс╣Зyaka 1.14), to him who has not prominent or vigorous life through the day, being dimmed or enfeebled by the superior effulgence of the sun

Jamison Brereton

This fortifying power of his might we acquire in future (days), of him who by night is more beautiful to see than by dayтАФ(more beautiful to see) than the one who traverses by day [=sun], for (the man) whose lifespan is not (yet) extended,294 I.127
because his [=AgniтАЩs] lifespan provides a handhold, staunch like shelter for a son.
His help, apportioned (to us?) or not, the unaging ones are pursuingтАФ the unaging fires are pursuing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the respite of vs. 4, this verse returns to puns and word plays in full force. The syntax of this verse is complicated enough without unintended ambiguity in the English. In the pub. tr. тАЬThis fortifying power of his might we acquire тАжтАЭ тАШmightтАЩ is a modal verb (тАЬmight we acquireтАЭ), not an abstract noun (*тАЬhis mightтАЭ).

In my opinion the hapax d├нv─Бtar─Бt in bc is a ┼Ыleс╣гa somewhat like druhaс╣Гtar├бс╕е in 3bc, again utilizing the echo p─Бda (c) to instantiate a 2nd value for a word found in both p─Бdas. Most take the word as a nonce substantivization of the adverb d├нv─Б by the addition of the comparative suffix found also in the preceding sud├бr┼Ыataraс╕е тАШmore beautifulтАЩ (see AiG II.2.608; Renou n. ad loc.). I agree that this is one reading, but I also think that -tara- can be a thematic nominal to тИЪtс╣Э тАШcross overтАЩ (cf. t├бra- etc.), and that the whole compound can mean тАШtraversing [the sky] by dayтАЩ as a descriptor of the sun. For a similarly formed rhyme word, also referring to the sun, cf. div─Бkar├б- тАШday-makerтАЩ (AV+).

The hapax ├бpr─Бyuс╣гe in c also poses difficulties. On the one hand, it is very similar to ├бpr─Бyu- (3x) тАШunremitting, not falteringтАЩ, which most deriv from pr├б тИЪyu; Oldenberg and Renou opt for this analysis (Renou тАЬ├а (lтАЩhomme qui veille) infatigableтАЭ). However, I am persuaded by GeldnerтАЩs pointing out (n. 5) the unity of theme provided by ├бpr─Бyuс╣гe (c) тАж ─Б╠Бyuс╕е (d) тАж aj├бr─Бс╕е (fg), if ├бpr─Бyuс╣гe contains the тАШlifetimeтАЩ word. However, I do not think either GeldnerтАЩs тАЬohne zu alternтАЭ or Witzel Got┼НтАЩs тАЬzum Nichtverschwinden der LebenskraftтАЭ is the correct analysis. Rather I think the word evokes the common idiom ─Б╠Бyuс╕е pra тИЪtс╣Э тАШlengthen lifetimeтАЩ and refers to a man whose lifetime has not yet been lengthened. Note that the тИЪtс╣Э part of the idiom can be pulled out of d├нv─Бtara- (a 3rd sense for this compound). Agni is called vi┼Ыv─Б╠Бyu- тАШproviding/affording all lifetimesтАЩ in the next hymn (I.128.8) and is also regularly asked to lengthen (pr├б тИЪtс╣Э ) our lifespan (e.g., I.94.16, VIII.44.30). I now also believe that ├бpr─Бyu- also contains the тАШlifetimeтАЩ word (the less well-attested ─Б╠Бyu- beside ─Б╠Бyus-); see comm. ad V.80.3.

In the next p─Бda AgniтАЩs own lifespan (that is, his immortality, more explicit in fg) is a model for our own: it provides a handhold (gr├бbhaс╣Зavat) or, as we would say, тАЬa leg upтАЭ for the man hoping to have his lifespan extended.

I donтАЩt quite understand bhakt├бm ├бbhaktaс╣Г v─Б. It is probably an implicitly temporal expression: the help that has already been apportioned and the rest that has not yet been apportioned (but will be, we hope).

Griffith

Here near we place the sacrificial food for him who shines forth fairer in the night than in the day, with life then stronger than by day.
His life gives sure and firm defence as that one giveth to a son.
The during fires enjoy things given and things not given, the during fires enjoy as food.

Oldenberg

Let us place that power 1 of his in our neighbourhood 2тАФ(that power) which is more visible by night than by day 3тАФ(more visible) than by day to the unremitting 4 (worshipper). Therefore his life is a firm hold 5, like (a father’s) safe refuge to a son: (the fires) that never grow old, tending to blessings enjoyed or not enjoyed (before) 6тАФthe fires that never grow old, tending (to such blessings).

Nach geschenkter und ungeschenkter Gunst verlangend sind die alterlosen Flammen, verlangend die alterlosen Agni┬┤s.

In seine N├дhe bringen wir dies Labeross, ihm, der bei Nacht noch heller als bei Tage strahlt, nicht rastend, als bei Tage strahlt, Sein Leben bietet starken Halt, fest wie dem Sohn des Vaters Schutz; Geschenktes, ungeschenktes speisend altern nicht die Flammen, nimmer altern sie.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe roars aloud, like the roaring of the winds, amidst the sanctified and selected (rites of sacred) solemnities; he who is to be worshipped, who is to be adored (for victory) over hosts (of enemies); he, the receiver 9of oblations), the manifester of the sacrifice; he, who is deserving of veneration, devours the oblations; hence, all men for their good pursue the path of Agni, who gives plural asure (to his worshipper), being plural ased (himself), in like manner as men follow a path (that leads) to happiness.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For he is very noisy like the Marut troop, thundering widely in the productive meadowsтАФthundering widely in the disorderly meadows. The taker has taken, has eaten the oblations, as is his due, he the beacon of the sacrifice.
And then when he is excited, bristling with excitement, all take pleasure in his pathтАФas the superior men [=Maruts] (take pleasure) in the path to beauty.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verse has an extra p─Бda (h), which serves as the tag-p─Бda to g. Given the difficulties in the verse, the extra p─Бda just provides more occasion for bewilderment.

The hapax iс╣гс╣н├бni- in the paired p─Бdas bc has been variously interpreted. Grassmann takes it to (n)is + тИЪstan тАШthunderтАЩ (тАШthunderтАЩ explicitly rejected by Oldenberg). Geldner does not comment but his tr. тАШsich ausbreitendтАЩ suggests a derivation from тИЪtan тАШstretchтАЩ; his tr. is echoed by Renou (тАШsтАЩ├йtendantтАЩ), though in his n. he suggests that the first element is the zero-grade root noun to тИЪyaj тАШsacrificeтАЩ, encouraged by Oldenberg The currently prevailing interpr. is probably HoffmannтАЩs (reported in KEWA, EWA) тАШspreading nourishmentтАЩ, found in Witzel Got┼Н. This is certainly possible; however, I favor тИЪstan тАШthunderтАЩ, despite OldenbergтАЩs disapproval, but with the preverb v├н. The Saс╣Гhit─Б text reads тАж urv├бr─Бsviс╣гс╣н├бnir (b) / ─Б╠Бrtan─Бsviс╣гс╣н├бniс╕еi (c), but both loc. plurals require metrical distraction: urv├бr─Бs u viс╣гс╣н├бnir (etc.). The Pp. reads urv├бr─Бsu / iс╣гt├бniс╕е (etc.), but nothing prevents reading urv├бr─Бsu / viс╣гt├бniс╕е from the distracted -s(u)vi- sequence. Although vi тИЪstan is not found until very late, it would not be a difficult idiom to create, esp.

given the widespread v├н тИЪdyut тАШflash forth as lightningтАЩ in the same pragmatic sphere.

The thunder would thematically continue the noise of the first p─Бda and the association with the Maruts, storm gods.

P─Бda c contains a 2nd hapax, ─Б╠Бrtan─Бsu, which both Geldner and Witzel Got┼Н refuse to tr.

(though see Witzel Got┼Н n. for a different suggestion) and Oldenberg, having offered a few suggestions, refuses to analyze. Renou tr. тАЬles terres sterilesтАЭ but without comment (though the tr. probably stems from GrassmannтАЩs тАШ├╝bel, ├╢de, Misernten bringendтАЩ). My own suggestion is quite speculative, but in this situation there seems no other choice. The p─Бda is a syllable short; Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition in fact divide up the first vowel, reading ─Б╠Б├бrtan─Бsu, but a stem ├бrtan─Б- does us no more good than ─Б╠Бrtan─Б-. I suggest supplying the syllable nir to open the p─Бda (and the word, hence *nir─Б╠Бrtan─Бsu); this nir can be generated from the final syllable of the preceding p─Бda (iс╣гс╣н├бn)nir, or rather we can imagine a haplology: iс╣гс╣н├бnir, *nir─Б╠Бrtan─Бsu. This posited stem *nir─Б╠Бrtan─Б- would belong to n├нr тИЪс╣Ы, most prominent in the well-attested n├нrс╣Ыti- тАШchaos, disorder, dissolutionтАЩ. The loc. pl. pairing in bc would then contrast the productive (├бpnasvant-) fields/meadows with their negative counterpart, disorderly and useless.

Note the alliteration in d: ─Б╠Бdad dhavy─Б╠Бny ─Бdad├нr, followed by ├бdha beginning f (as well as ─Б╠Бd beginning 5d).

As Geldner points out (n. 6d), ─Б╠Бdat can be the impf. to тИЪad тАШeatтАЩ as well as belonging to ─Б╠БтИЪd─Б тАШtakeтАЩ, though he doesnтАЩt incorporate this pun into his tr. Agni as the eater of oblations is of course a common trope.

h├бrс╣гato hс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─лvataс╕е in f is a nice etymological figure, though in the context of this hymn barely deserving mention.

Most tr. take the n├бraс╕е of h as ordinary, human men, but I think it refers rather to the Maruts. ┼Ыubh├й (and ┼Ы├║bh- in general) is one of their signature words; cf., e.g., I.88.2 ┼Ыubh├й k├бm y─Бnti and, with n├бraс╕е referring to them, V.52.8 тАж t├й ┼Ыubh├й n├бraс╕е. The mention of the Maruts here would form a ring with their appearance in p─Бda a.

Griffith

He, roaring very loudly like the Maruts’ host, in fertile cultivated fields adorable, in desert spots adorable,
Accepts and eats our offered gifts, ensign of sacrifice by desert;
So let all, joying, love his path when he is glad, as men pursue a path for bliss.

Oldenberg

He indeed makes a mighty noise like the host of the Maruts, тАж 1 on the rich fields, тАж 1 on the тАж 1. He, the seizer, ate the offerings 2, he who has deservedly become the banner of the sacrifice. And when he joyously and joyfully (proceeds), all followed gladly on his path; men (have followed) his path as for a triumphal procession.

Geldner

Denn er ist lautrauschend gleich der marutischen Heerschar in den ertragreichen Feldern sich ausbreitend, in den ………..sich ausbreitend. Der Nehmer hat die Opferspenden an sich genommen, wie sich┬┤s geb├╝hrt, er des Opfers Wahrzeichen. Dann, wenn er freudig, ungeduldig ist, haben alle an seinem Wege ihr Wohlgefallen wie die Herren an dem Wege zur Prunkfahrt.

Grassmann

Denn er ist m├дchtig, rauschend wie die Marutschar, auf wohlbebauten Ackerfeldern brauset er, auf ├╢den Fl├дchen brauset er; Empfangend nahm die Tr├дnke er, des Opfers Banner, nach Geb├╝hr; Wenn er sich freut, der freudenreiche, m├╢gen sich an seinem Gange alle freun. (die M├дnner alle wie zur Pracht.)

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe descendants of Bhс╣Ыgu, celebrating him (Agni) in both his forms, glorifying him, and payig him homage, proclaim his praises; the descendants of Bhс╣Ыgu, rubbing (the flame) for the oblation. For the radiant Agni, who is the guardian of all these treasures, has power (to distribute them). Mayhe, the receier of sacrifices, partake of the agreeable (offerings) given to satiety; may he, the receiver of sacrifices, partake (of the oblations).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dvit─Б yad im kr─лst─Бsaс╕е, celebrating him as twofold; i.e. either as recognized in both the ┼Ъruti and Smс╣Ыti, the books of religion and law; or, as the giver of happiness in both this world and the next; or, as manifold in the ─Аhavan─лha and other fires, ’two’ connoting multiple or many

Jamison Brereton

When, yet again, the heaven-bound praisers, the Bhr╠еgus, tendering homage, invoke himтАФthe Bhr╠еgus, plundering (the fire from heaven), churning it with pietyтАФ
Agni is lord of goods, the blazing one who is their holderтАФ
then his dear coverings the wise one should seek to winтАФthe wise one should seek to win here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most take k─лst├б- in p─Бda as a PN, a further specification of the Bhс╣Ыgus, and this is a tempting way to avoid dealing with the word. However, it is more difficult to take it as a PN in its only other appearance in the RV (and indeed anywhere) at VI.67.10. I therefore follow the interpr. going back at least to S─Бyaс╣Зa, тАШpraiserтАЩ. EWA has a reasonably plausible scenario for getting it as a hypersanskritization of a MIA form of *k─лrtha-, beside k─лrt├н- тАШpraiseтАЩ, etc.

I take mathn├бntaс╕е in c as a pun on тИЪmath тАШstealтАЩ (referring to the Bhс╣ЫgusтАЩ theft of fire; see Narten, KlSch. 23-24) and тАШchurn, rubтАЩ, a common word for the production of the fire on the ritual ground.

The identity of the тАЬdear coveringsтАЭ is not clear. Geldner suggest, for example, that they are what keep Agni within the kindling sticks, Witzel Got┼Н that they are everything a fire burning in a field would incorporate in itself. Since Agni is identified as the holder (dharс╣З├н-) of goods in e, I wonder if the coverings are the enclosure itself – though what this means physically IтАЩm not sure.

On the isolated precative vaniс╣г─лс╣гс╣нa see Narten (SigAor. 236-37), who points out that its object is also a hapax and considers it an тАЬAugenblicksbildung des Dichters.тАЭ The тАЬwise oneтАЭ (m├йdhira-) is probably Agni himself, as often, and the med. form of the verb would support this identification.

Griffith

Even as they who sang forth hymns, addressed to heaven, the Bhrgus with their prayer and praise invited him, the Bhrgus rubbing, offering gifts.
For radiant Agni, Lord of all these treasures, is exceeding strong.
May he, the wise, accept the grateful coverings, the wise accept the coverings.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe invoke you, the protector of all people, the same alike to all, the preserver of the house, to enjoy (the oblation); you, who are the wafter of our infallible prayer, to enjoy (the oblation); we invoke you, who are the guest of men, to whom all these immortals apply for their sustenance, as (a son) to a father; you, to whom the priests offer oblations amongst the gods.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We invoke you, lord of all the clans, houselord common to every one of them, for benefitтАФyou with your trusty vehicle of songs, for benefitтАФ
the guest of the sons of Manu, by whose mouth, as if by a fatherтАЩs, (we) and all the immortals yonder (acquire) vigorтАФ(place) the
oblations and vigor among the gods.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse begins straightforwardly enough but its syntax deteriorates (or gets more convoluted) towards the end.

The three-member cmpd. saty├бgirv─Бhas- in c is implicitly analyzed by Geldner as saty├бgir-v─Бhas- (тАЬihn den wahrhafte Reden anziehenтАЭ; sim. Witzel Got┼Н), but, on the one hand, g├нrv─Бhas- is an established bahuvr─лhi (8x; тАЬwhose vehicle is songsтАЭ – that is, the god [Indra] who is conveyed to the sacrifice by the songs dedicated to him) and, on the other, saty├б- never modifies g├нr- as far as I can tell. Oldenberg (SBE) tr. тАЬwho truly art carried by prayers as by a vehicle,тАЭ with the correct internal structure, in my opinion. My тАЬtrustyтАЭ for saty├б- may be pushing the term a bit, but the idea is that the song-vehicle is real and so a trustworthy conveyance.

The ca in f is generally rendered тАШalsoтАЩ, and it is one of only three examples (out of approx. 1100) of ca to which Klein (DGRV I.212-13) attributes that value.

None of the examples is strong, and all can be interpreted with functional values more commonly found with ca. In this case I think am─л╠Бca v├н┼Ыve amс╣Ы╠Бt─Бsaс╕е is conjoined with a gapped vay├бm тАШweтАЩ, as in exx. like VII.88.3 ─Б╠Бy├бd ruh─Б╠Бva v├бruс╣Зa┼Ы ca n─Б╠Бvam тАЬWhen [I] and Varuс╣Зa boarded the boat тАж,тАЭ though with pl. rather than sg.

1st ps. gapping. The 1st ps. pl. is found in the opening verb of the verse hav─Бmahe, and although some p─Бdas intervene, that main verb still has domain over the whole verse (save for the last p─Бda), with ef a rel. cl. attached to that main clause. True, the verb in this rel. clause must also be supplied. I suggest a medial form of тИЪdh─Б, meaning тАШacquireтАЩ; see in fact dh─лmahi in this meaning in 5a – all that is needed is an accent.

For the identical VP v├бyas- + med. тИЪdh─Б in this same hymn cycle, cf. I.136.2 ├бth─Б dadh─Бte тАж v├бyaс╕е тАЬthen they two [=Mitra and Varuс╣Зa] acquire vigor,тАЭ and for a 1st pl.

in this collocation (including the instr.) see II.23.10 tv├бy─Б vay├бm uttam├бс╣Г dh─лmahe v├бyaс╕е тАЬThrough you might we acquire the utmost vigor.тАЭ In nearby I.141.13 (though not a Paruchepa hymn) am─л╠Бca is overtly conjoined with vay├бm, as I suggest is covertly the case here: am─л╠Бca y├й magh├бv─Бno vay├бс╣Г ca тАЬthose who are our patrons and we (ourselves) тАжтАЭ As for p─Бda g, which also lacks a verb, my published translation assumes an active imperatival form of the same root тИЪdh─Б, addressed to Agni. Agni quite regularly participates in such collocations; in this case the verb might well be the imperativally used root aor. injunctive dh─Бс╕е or else the redupl. pres. impv. dhehi. This short p─Бda blends two constructions: тАЬset oblations among LOCтАЭ and тАЬestablish vigor for DAT,тАЭ both with тИЪdh─Б. For the first, with Agni as subject, see, e.g., V.14.1 havy─Б╠Бdev├йс╣гu no dadhat; for the second, likewise with Agni as subject, see, e.g., II.4.9 sm├бt s┼лr├нbhyo gс╣Ыс╣Зat├й t├бd v├бyo dh─Бс╕е тАЬestablish this vigor for the singer along with his patrons.тАЭ Since in our passage the recipients of the v├бyas- have already been identified in the previous p─Бda ([us] and all the immortals), the dative recipient with the second construction need not be specified. A more literal tr. of my understanding of this p─Бda might then be тАЬ(place) the oblations among the gods and (establish) vigor,тАЭ but this seemed too clotted for the published translation

The trick of this tag-p─Бda then is that the final ─Б╠Бv├бyaс╕е is twice the object of an unexpressed form of the root тИЪdh─Б, but with two different valences. Unusually for tag-p─Бdas, g is not syntactically parallel to f.

Griffith

Thee we invoke, the Lord of all our settled homes, common to all, the household’s guardian, to enjoy, bearer of true hymns, to enjoy.
Thee we invoke, the guest of men, by whose mouth, even as a sire’s,
All these Immortals come to gain their food of life, oblations come to Gods as food.

Oldenberg

We invoke thee, the lord of all people, the common master of the house of all, to enjoy (the sacrifice): (we call) thee who truly art carried by prayers as by a vehicle 1 to enjoy (the sacrifice): the guest of men in whose presence (they live) as before a father’s (face), and all those immortals (attain) to strength, and the offerings among the gods (attain) to strength.

Geldner

Dich den Herren aller St├дmme rufen wir an, den gemeinsamen Gebieter aller St├дmme uns zu Nutz, ihn den wahrhafte Reden anziehen, zu Nutz, den Gast der Menschen, durch dessen Mund wie durch den eines Vaters, auch alle jene Unsterblichen ihre St├дrkung empfangen und die Opfer als St├дrkung zu den G├╢ttern gelangen.

Grassmann

Dich rufen wir, den Herren aller St├дmme, her, den einen Hausherrn aller St├дmme zum Genuss, den Liederherren zum Genuss, Der du der Gast der Menschen bist, und vor uns wie ein Vater stehst; Es m├╢gen alle jene G├╢tter kommen her zum Mahl, und Tr├дnke zu dem G├╢ttermahl.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕рд╣рд╕рд╛ рдмрд▓реЗрди рд╕рд╣рдиреНрддрдордГ рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдорднрд┐рднрд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рддрдерд╛ рд╢реБрд╖реНрдорд┐рдиреНрддрдордГ рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА рдЬрд╛рдпрд╕реЗ рее рд╕рд╣реЗрд░реМрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдГ рдХрдирд┐рдиреН ред тАШрдирд╛рджреНрдзрд╕реНрдп’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдиреБрдЯреН ред рдХрд┐рдорд░реНрдердореН ред рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рддрдпреЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╕реНрддрд╛рд░рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдп рдпрд╛рдЧрд╛рдп рддрджрд░реНрдердореН ред рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдЙрдХреНрддрдЧреБрдгрд╡рд┐рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдГ рд╕ рдЬрд╛рдпрд╕реЗ ред рдЕрд░рдгреНрдпреЛрд░реБрддреНрдкрджреНрдпрд╕реЗ ред рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрдерддреНрд╡реЗ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рд░рдпрд┐рд░реНрди рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рддрдпреЗ ред рдзрдирдВ рдпрдерд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрдердореБрддреНрдкрджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪреЛрдХреНрддрдВ– тАШ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдореБрддреНрдкрдиреНрдирдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдорджрдГ рдЖрдЬреНрдпрд╕реНрд╡реАрдХрд╛рд░рдЬрдирд┐рддреЛ рд╣рд░реНрд╖рдГ! Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou, Agni, the destroyer (of enemies) by your strength, the possessor of great splendour, as born for the sake of sacrificing to the gods, as riches (are genitive rated) for the sake of sacrificing to the gods; verily your exhilaration is most brilliant, your worship is most productive of renown; hence, undecaying Agni, (sacrificers) wait upon you, like envoys (upon a prince; upon you), who preserve (your votaries) from decay.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ajara = undecaying, not causing decay; or, one who does not praise others; one to whom along praise is due

Jamison Brereton

You, Agni, are born as strongest by your strength, most tempestuous, for the divine conclaveтАФlike wealth for the divine conclaveтАФ
for most tempestuous is your exuberance and most brilliant your resolveтАФ
and then they attentively surround you, o unaging oneтАФlike obedient (servants), o unaging one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax splv. s├бhantama- does not require the positing (with Grassmann) of an otherwise unattested n-stem s├бhan-. A nonce derivation from the pres. part. s├бhant- (with simplification of the cluster s├бhan(t)-tama-, with AiG II.2.597, etc.) is certainly possible, and the full grade with nasal might have been constructed as a partial match for its parallels ┼Ыuс╣гm├нntama- and dyumn├нntama-.

I.127.9-10: The ends of both a-p─Бdas are variants of each other: 9a тАж s├бhas─Б s├бhantamaс╕е, 10a тАж s├бhas─Б s├бhasvate, each following a metrical rest.

Griffith

Thou, Agni, most victorious with thy conquering strength, most Mighty One, art born for service of the Gods, like wealth for service of the Gods.
Most mighty is thine ecstasy, most splendid is thy mental power.
Therefore men wait upon thee, undecaying One, like vassals, undecaying One.

Oldenberg

Thou, O Agni, art born, the mightiest by might 1, for the divine world, the strongest one, like wealth for the divine world. For thy delight is most strong, and thy power is most brilliant. And they walk around thee 2, O (god) who never growest old, like obedient (servants), O (god) who never growest old.

Geldner

Grassmann

O Agni du, als kr├дftigster an Siegeskraft, als m├дchtiger wirst du erzeugt zum Gottesdienst, wie Reichthum zu dem Gottesdienst, Dein Rausch ist ja der m├дchtigste, dein Wille ist der kr├дftigste, Drum huldigen dir alle, der du nie verlischst, wie Diener, der du nie verlischst.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay your praise, (oс╕е priests), become grateful to Agni, who is desrving of laudation, who is of strength to overcome the strong, who is awakened at the dawn; to Agni, as if to a giver of cattle. Inasmuch as the presenter of the oblation repairs assiduously to every altar, the invoking priest, well-skilled in (pious) praise, glorifies him (Agni) as the first of the attaining (divinities), as a herald (recites the praises) of illustrious (men).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The last p─Бda: lit. ‘in front, a herald, like praisers of the illustrious (с╣Ыс╣г┼лс╣З─Бm)

Jamison Brereton

Let your (praise) (stand) out for the great one, who is strong by strength, wakening at dawn, for Agni, as if for a winner of cattleтАФlet (your) praise stand (out) for Agni.
When someone with an oblation is calling on him in all the lands, in advance of (dawnтАЩs) rays he тАЬsingsтАЭ [=crackles] like a hoarse-voiced (singer)тАФthe glowing Hotar, (in advance of) the rays.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first three p─Бdas are an esp. nice example of the syntactic complementarity between the tag-p─Бda c and what precedes. The subject and the verb are withheld until c (st├│maс╕е and babh┼лtu respectively), with the preverb determining the verbal lexeme (pr├б) and the possessive pronoun limiting the praise (vaс╕е) found in the first p─Бda – and the recipient agn├бye the only thing held in common between ab and c. Thus neither ab nor c is complete in itself: their elements need to be intermingled to produce the full sense. The name of the recipient is also held until the end of the two-p─Бda opening, though prepared for by a series of datives.

Schaeffer (Inten. 114) argues persuasively that the intens. joguve is тАЬlokaldistributivтАЭ with the loc. phrase v├н┼Ыv─Бsu kс╣г─Б╠Бsu тАЬin all lands.тАЭ

Griffith

To him the mighty, conquering with victorious strength, to Agni walking with the dawn, who sendeth kine, be sung your laud, to Agni sung;
As he who with oblation comes calls him aloud in every place.
Before the brands of fire he shouteth singerlike, the herald, kindler of the brands.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, do youur becoming visible close to us, and partaking with benignant intent of (the sacrificial) food along with the gods, bestow upon us abundant riches, with benignant intent. Most mighty Agni, render us illustrious, that we may behold and enjoy (this earth); and grant greatness with excellent progeny to those who praise you, possessor of wealth, destroyer of foes, like a fierce (giant) in strength.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ugra na savasa: ka┼Ыcin kr┼лra, some one cruel or fierce

Jamison Brereton

Becoming visible in the nearest nearness, bring here to us, o Agni, in concert with the gods, (riches) through your kind attentionтАФgreat riches through your kind attention.
Make us regard something great, o most powerful one, for our
benefit here.
Plunder, churn a great mass of good heroes for the praisers, liberal oneтАФlike a mighty (warrior) with vast power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The latter part of this verse shows a nice phonological pattern, with the initial words in the p─Бda being c mah├│, d m├бhi, f m├бhi, but g m├бth─лr. The first three all belong of course to the mah (тАШgreatтАЩ) family, but the last is a verb form whose apparent near match with the two preceding m├бhi belies its independent grammatical identity.

There is probably also a phonological impetus for the use of s├бcanas- instead of the much more common saj├│с╣гas- in b: s├бcan─Бs better matches sucet├║n─Б.

In de most tr. (including me) take m├бhi тАж nas kс╣Ыdhi, saс╣Гc├бkс╣гe тАж as an infinitive phrase, тАЬmake us regard (something) great.тАЭ Keydana (Infin. 342) allows this possibility, but also raises the possibility of an adjunct usage: тАЬmake something great for us, for seeing.тАЭ Although I recognize that the latter is not excluded, I think the infinitive reading is the more likely – on the basis of the other dative phrase in e, bhuj├й asya├н. The final position of asya├н here is odd, and in fact the use of it at all is odd, given that an unadorned bhuj├й ends 8b and its tag-p─Бda 8c. I think that we have a demonstrative adj. with bhuj├й in this verse in order to anchor bhuj├й as a noun and to distinguish it from the immediately preceding dative, also built to a root noun, but in infinitival function. In other words, the asya├н serves to polarize the grammatical functions of two identically formed nominals.

In m├бth─лс╕е I see the same pun on the two roots тИЪmath as was found in 7c. Here the plundering sense is appropriate to the simile ugr├│ n├б ┼Ы├бvas─Б тАЬlike a mighty (warrior) with vast power,тАЭ while the churn sense is attached to Agni as fire the substance. Although the ritual fire is churned (passively), we can imagine Agni using the same means that produced him (churning) to produce something for us. (So, more or less, Geldner) Narten (KlSch 24; followed apparently by Witzel Got┼Н) feels that m├бth─лс╕е here can only have the тАШrobтАЩ sense, because only fire can be the obj. of the тАШchurnтАЩ sense, but this opinion displays, at least in my view, the often deficient poetic and imaginative sense of the Erlangen school.

Griffith

Agni, beheld by us in nearest neighbourhood, accordant with the Gods, bring us, with gracious love, great riches with thy gracious love.
Give us O Mightiest, what is great, to see and to enjoy the earth.
As one of awful power, stir up heroic might for those who praise thee, Bounteous Lord!

Oldenberg

Thus being seen by us, bring near to us, O Agni, graciously united with the gods, benignantly, great wealth benignantly. Make us behold great (bliss of valiant offspring 1), O mightiest one, that we may obtain such enjoyment. Produce great bliss of valiant offspring, O bountiful Lord, (as fire is produced) by attrition, for those who praise thee, like a strong hero in thy might.

Geldner

Der du in n├дchster N├дhe erscheinst, bring, Agni, uns eintr├дchtig mit den G├╢ttern aus Wohlwollen gro├Яe Reicht├╝mer aus Wohlwollen! La├Я uns, M├дchtigster, Gro├Яes schauen um dies zu genie├Яen. Reib uns S├дngern, du Freigebiger, gro├Яe gute Sohnschaft heraus, wie ein Starker das Feuer mit Kraft austreibt.

Grassmann

In n├дchster N├дhe, Agni du, geschaut von uns, vereinigt mit den G├╢ttern bringe wohlgesinnt uns grossen Reichthum wohlgesinnt, Recht grosses lass, o kr├дftigster, uns sehen und geniessen hier, Errege grosse Heldenkraft, o m├дchtiger, den S├дngern, starker du an Kraft.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдлрд┐рд░ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдХреНрдпрд╛ рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ, рдЗрд╕ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдп рдХреЛ рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рд╛ рд╣реИ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ (рдордШрд╡рдиреН) рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рдд рдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрдд (рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрда) рдЕрддреАрд╡ рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рдпреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╣ (рджрджреГрд╢рд╛рдирдГ) рджреЗрдЦреЗ рд╣реБрдП рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН ! рдЖрдк (рд╕реБрдЪреЗрддреБрдирд╛) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рд╕рдордЭрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдФрд░ (рджреЗрд╡реЗрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдорд╣рдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдд (рд╕рдЪрдирд╛рдГ) рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдз рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рдзрдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЖ, рднрд░) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░реЗрдВ (рдЕрд╕реНрдпреИ) рдЗрд╕ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╕рдВрдЪрдХреНрд╖реЗ) рдЙрддреНрддрдорддрд╛ рдореЗрдВ рдХрд╣рдиреЗ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рджреЗрдиреЗ рдФрд░ (рднреБрдЬреЗ) рдЗрд╕рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛) рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рд╕реЗ (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдЪрдгреНрдб рдкреНрд░рддрд╛рдкрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рди) рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди (рдордереАрдГ) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдордердиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЖрдк (рдиреЗрджрд┐рд╖реНрдардореН) рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрдд рд╕рдореАрдк (рдорд╣рд┐) рдмрд╣реБрдд (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░реНрдпрдореН) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдо рдХреЛ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░реЛ рдФрд░ рдЗрд╕ (рд╕реБрдЪреЗрддреБрдирд╛) рд╕реБрдиреНрджрд░ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЧреБрдг рд╕реЗ (рдорд╣рд┐) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХрддрд╛ рд╕реЗ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╣реЛ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ (рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ) рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╢рдВрд╕рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдирдГ) рд╣рдо рд▓реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдХреГрдзрд┐) рдХрд░реЛ рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рдФрд░ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИрдВред рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рдХрд┐ рд╕рдХрд▓ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рдкрдврд╝реЗ рд╣реБрдП рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреЛрдВ рдХреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердирд╛ рдФрд░ рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░ рдкреВрд░реА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рд╡реЗрдВ, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрди рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдзрд░реНрдо рдХрд╛ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдХрд░реЗрдВ рее резрез реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдФрд░ рд░рд╛рдЬрдзрд░реНрдо рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдПрдХрддрд╛ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ рее рдпрд╣ рдПрдХрд╕реМ рд╕рддреНрддрд╛рдИрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рддреЗрд░рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рд╣реЗ рдордШрд╡рдиреН рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдард╛рдЧреНрдиреЗ рд╕ рджрджреГрд╢рд╛рдирд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реБрдЪреЗрддреБрдирд╛ рджреЗрд╡реЗрднрд┐рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рд╣ рдиреЛ рдорд╣рдГ рд╕рдЪрдирд╛ рд░рд╛рдп рдЖрднрд░рд╛рд╕реНрдпреИ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдпреИ рд╕рдВрдЪрдХреНрд╖реЗ рднреБрдЬреЗ рд╢рд╡рд╕реЛрдЧреНрд░реЛ рди рдордереАрд╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рдиреЗрджрд┐рд╖реНрдардВ рдорд╣рд┐ рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░реНрдпрдорд╛рднрд░рд╛рд╜рдиреЗрди рд╕реБрдЪреЗрддреБрдирд╛ рдорд╣рд┐ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпреЛ рдиреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рддрдГ рдХреГрдзрд┐ рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдкреБрдирд░реНрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдХрд┐рдВ рдХрд░реНрддреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рд╕рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдореН (рдиреЗрджрд┐рд╖реНрдардореН) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрдирд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдХрдореН (рджрджреГрд╢рд╛рдирдГ) рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдиреН (рдЖ) рд╕рдордиреНрддрд╛рддреН (рднрд░) рдзрд░ (рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗ) рдкрд╛рд╡рдХ рдЗрд╡ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рди (рджреЗрд╡реЗрднрд┐рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рджреНрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рд╣ (рд╕рдЪрдирд╛рдГ) рд╕рдорд╡реЗрддреБрдВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрд╛рдГ (рд╕реБрдЪреЗрддреБрдирд╛) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБрд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреНрд░рд╛ (рдорд╣рдГ) рдорд╣рддрдГ (рд░рд╛рдпрдГ) рдзрдирд╛рдирд┐ (рд╕реБрдЪреЗрддреБрдирд╛) рд╕реБрд╖реНрдареБ рдЪреЗрддрдпрд┐рддреНрд░рд╛ (рдорд╣рд┐) рдорд╣рддреН (рд╢рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрда) рдЕрддрд┐рд╢рдпреЗрди рдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╡рд┐рджреНрдп (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН (рдХреГрдзрд┐) рдХреБрд░реБ (рд╕рдВрдЪрдХреНрд╖реЗ) рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдп (рднреБрдЬреЗ) рдкрд╛рд▓рдирд╛рдп (рдЕрд╕реНрдпреИ) рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдпреИ (рдорд╣рд┐) рдорд╣рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ (рд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрднреНрдпрдГ) (рдордШрд╡рдиреН) рдкреВрдЬрд┐рддрдзрдирдпреБрдХреНрдд (рд╕реБрд╡реАрд░реНрдпрдореН) рд╢реЛрднрдирдВ рдкрд░рд╛рдХреНрд░рдордореН (рдордереАрдГ) рдпрд╛ рджреБрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреН рдордереНрдирд╛рддрд┐ рд╕рдГ (рдЙрдЧреНрд░рдГ) рддреЗрдЬрд╕реНрд╡реА (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рд╢рд╡рд╕рд╛) рдмрд▓реЗрди рее резрез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░реМред рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рднрд┐рд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛рдирдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рдиреН рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдереНрдп рд╕рдВрд╕реЗрд╡реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрдгрд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдгреАрдпрд╛рдГред рдпреЗрди рд░рд╛рдЬрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдЬрдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдиреНрддреЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рддрддрдВ рдзрд░реНрдордорд╛рдЪрд░реЗрдпреБрдГ рее резрез реердЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рддреНрд░рдпреЛрджрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдпрд╛ рдордВрддреНрд░рд╛рдд рдЙрдкрдорд╛ рд╡ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдВрдХрд╛рд░ рдЖрд╣реЗрдд. рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рдВрдиреА рд╕рдВрдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рд╢рд┐рдХрд▓реЗрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рдзрд╛рд░реНрдорд┐рдХ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдЪреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердирд╛ рд╡ рд╕реЗрд╡рд╛ рдХрд░реВрди рдкреВрд░реНрдг рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реА. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛ рд╡ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдпрд╛рдВрдиреА рд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╣реЛрдКрди рдирд┐рд░рдВрддрд░ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рдЪреЗ рдЖрдЪрд░рдг рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рее резрез рее
